## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / theoretical biology
**Analysis**: The task models population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of population size (P) and time (t). It belongs to population ecology, where density-dependent regulation, carrying capacity, and time-varying factors are key. The expected relationships include sigmoidal saturation, Allee effects, and growth modulated by resource limitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth)
- Logistic differential: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) (density-dependent saturation)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoid, often for tumor/ageing)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (metabolic scaling, e.g., c1=2/3 for mass)
- Richards generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (shape parameter tunes asymmetry)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P / c1 - 1) * (1 - P / c2) (cubic, positive growth only above threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) * (P / c2 - 1) (depensation, reduced but not negative at low P)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal forcing)
- Resource-consumer saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) / (c1 + c2 * P) (Type III functional response coexistence)
- Gompertz with time delay: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2 * t)) (time-decaying carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric growth when c1≠1)
- Exponential decay of per-capita growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (gradual slowdown independent of density)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P (constant effort harvesting)
- Density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (quadratic closure representing competition)
- Bimodal growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) * (P - c2) (alternative stable states, e.g., strong Allee plus carrying capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Hump-shaped dP/dt vs P curve → density-dependent regulation, typically logistic-like product P*(K-P) or its generalization
- Per-capita growth rate (1/P dP/dt) linearly declining with P → logistic or similar saturation mechanism
- Per-capita growth rate linearly declining with log(P) → Gompertz growth, often for age-dependent mortality or tumor growth
- Negative growth rate at very low P → Allee effect, requiring cubic or higher-order polynomial with a negative intercept
- Multiple equilibrium points (dP/dt=0 at several non-zero P) → strong Allee effect or alternative stable states, modeled by polynomial with multiple roots
- Time-varying coefficients in density-dependent terms → environmental seasonality or trend in carrying capacity
- Growth rate proportional to P raised to a fractional power → metabolic scaling laws (e.g., von Bertalanffy, allometry)
- Sudden flattening of dP/dt after exponential phase → resource depletion, captured by terms like (1 - P/K) or log(K/P)
- Smooth inflection point in the growth rate vs P → asymmetric sigmoid (Gompertz, Richards) where the inflection occurs at a fraction of carrying capacity
- Linear decrease in dP/dt with increasing P beyond a point → pure resource limitation without nonlinear feedback, dP/dt = r*P - a*P^2

Let me expand the first term:

Let me denote a = 6.058, b = 14.185 for brevity.

`(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P = (P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P`

Expanding `(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)`:
= `P/a - P²/(ab) - 1 + P/b`
= `-1 + P/a + P/b - P²/(ab)`

Multiplying by P:
= `-P + P²/a + P²/b - P³/(ab)`

`c * (-P + P²/a + P²/b - P³/(ab)) + c*P^(1/3) + c*P`
